Domain Examples

E-Commerce: Product Price Filter

User Story: As a customer, I want to filter products by price range, so that I can find items within my budget quickly.

Acceptance Criteria:

  1. Given products exist from $10–$500, when user sets min $50 and max $200 and applies filter, then only products in range display.
  2. Given user sets min > max, when applying filter, then show validation error and do not filter.
  3. Given active price filter, when user clicks "Clear Filters", then all products display and filter resets.
  4. Given filter applied, when user navigates away and returns, then filter persists in session.
  5. Given no products match range, when filter applied, then show "No products found" with clear option.

Test Scenarios Derived from AC:

IDScenarioType
TS-01Apply valid price range $50–$200; verify product count and pricesFunctional — Happy path
TS-02Set min $300, max $100; verify error messageNegative
TS-03Apply filter, click Clear; verify full catalog restoredFunctional
TS-04Apply filter, navigate to product detail, browser back; verify filter persistsSession/State
TS-05Filter $9999–$10000; verify empty state message and UIBoundary
TS-06Filter with min=$0; verify products at $0.01+ included appropriatelyBoundary
TS-07Concurrent filter: price + category; verify combined resultsIntegration

Banking: Money Transfer

User Story: As an account holder, I want to transfer money to another account, so that I can pay friends and family instantly.

Acceptance Criteria:

  1. Given sufficient balance, when user enters valid recipient account and amount, then transfer completes and both balances update within 30 seconds.
  2. Given insufficient balance, when user submits transfer, then show error "Insufficient funds" and no debit occurs.
  3. Given transfer amount exceeds daily limit ($10,000), when submitted, then block with limit message.
  4. Given successful transfer, when complete, then user receives confirmation with transaction ID and timestamp.
  5. Given invalid recipient account number, when submitted, then show "Account not found" without debiting sender.

Test Scenarios:

IDScenarioType
TS-01Transfer $100 from Account A ($500 balance) to valid Account B; verify balancesHappy path
TS-02Transfer $600 from Account A ($500 balance); verify rejectionNegative
TS-03Transfer $10,001 in single day; verify daily limit enforcementBoundary/Business rule
TS-04Complete transfer; verify confirmation email/SMS with transaction IDIntegration
TS-05Enter non-existent account number; verify no debit, error shownNegative
TS-06Transfer $0.01 (minimum); verify successBoundary
TS-07Concurrent transfers from same account totaling > balance; verify only one succeedsConcurrency/Security

Healthcare: Appointment Booking

User Story: As a patient, I want to book an appointment with my doctor online, so that I don't have to call the clinic during business hours.

Acceptance Criteria:

  1. Given patient is logged in, when selecting available slot from doctor's calendar, then appointment is confirmed and added to patient dashboard.
  2. Given slot was just booked by another patient, when current user submits, then show "Slot no longer available" and refresh calendar.
  3. Given appointment is 24+ hours away, when patient cancels, then slot reopens and confirmation email sent.
  4. Given appointment is within 24 hours, when patient attempts cancel, then show policy message and disable cancel button.
  5. Given booking complete, when confirmed, then send confirmation email with date, time, doctor name, and clinic address.

Test Scenarios:

IDScenarioType
TS-01Book available slot; verify dashboard, calendar update, confirmation emailHappy path
TS-02Two users book same slot simultaneously; verify one succeeds, one gets errorConcurrency
TS-03Cancel appointment 48 hours before; verify slot available, email sentFunctional
TS-04Attempt cancel 12 hours before; verify blocked per policyBusiness rule
TS-05Book without login; verify redirect to loginSecurity
TS-06Verify HIPAA: appointment details not visible to other patientsSecurity/Compliance

How QA Writes Test Cases from User Stories — Step-by-Step

  1. Read the story — understand persona, goal, and business value
  2. Review Acceptance Criteria — each AC should map to at least one test case
  3. Identify test scenarios — happy path, negative, boundary, integration, NFR (performance, security, accessibility)
  4. Apply equivalence partitioning and boundary value analysis — derive data sets from input rules
  5. Write test cases with: ID, title, preconditions, steps, expected result, priority, traceability to story/AC
  6. Review with PO/Dev — Three Amigos or async review for missed edge cases
  7. Prioritize — P1 for AC coverage, P2 for edge cases, P3 for exploratory charters
  8. Automate — convert Given-When-Then AC to Cucumber/Cypress/Playwright specs where ROI is high
  9. Execute and update — log results in Jira/Zephyr; update when AC changes

Bad vs Good User Story Comparison

AspectBad StoryGood Story
Format"Fix login""As a user, I want to reset my password via email, so that I can regain access if I forget it"
Testability"System should be user-friendly""Search results return in <2 seconds for 95th percentile"
Size"Build complete CRM module" (epic disguised as story)"As a sales rep, I want to add a note to a lead, so that I track conversation history"
AC QualityNo acceptance criteria3–5 Given-When-Then scenarios covering happy, negative, edge cases
Independence"Add checkout with loyalty, coupons, and gift cards"Split: three independent stories, prioritized separately
Value"Upgrade React to v18""As a user, I want faster page loads (tech enabler linked to perf epic)"
Persona"As a user..." (too generic)"As a premium subscriber..." (specific permissions/rules)
Estimability"Improve reporting""As a manager, I want to export monthly sales report as PDF"

Interview Questions & Answers — User Stories

Q1: What is a user story and how is it formatted?

A: A brief requirement from the user's perspective: "As a [user], I want [functionality], so that [benefit]." Details are in AC and conversations.

Q2: Explain INVEST principles.

A: Independent, Negotiable, Valuable, Estimable, Small, Testable — criteria for well-formed stories. QA especially cares about Testable and Small.

Q3: What are Acceptance Criteria and how do you write them?

A: Conditions of satisfaction for a story. Use Given-When-Then for clarity and automation. Each AC should be verifiable pass/fail. QA collaborates with PO to write them during refinement.

Q4: What are story points and how do they differ from hours?

A: Relative measure of effort/complexity using Fibonacci scale. Not time — a 5-point story is ~2.5x a 2-point story. Accounts for dev, test, and integration complexity.

Q5: What is Planning Poker?

A: Estimation technique where team members vote privately with cards, reveal together, discuss outliers, and converge. QA ensures test complexity is considered.

Q6: Epic vs Feature vs Story vs Task — explain hierarchy.

A: Epic = large initiative spanning sprints. Feature = cohesive capability within epic. Story = single sprint-sized user value. Task = breakdown work item for dev/QA within a story.

Q7: How do you derive test cases from a user story?

A: Map each AC to test cases; add negative, boundary, integration, and NFR scenarios; apply test design techniques; trace test IDs to story; prioritize and automate high-value paths.

Q8: What makes a user story "testable"?

A: Clear, measurable AC with defined inputs and expected outputs. Avoid subjective terms ("fast," "easy"). Specific thresholds and error messages enable pass/fail determination.

Q9: Give an example of splitting a large story.

A: "User registration" epic splits into: (1) Register with email/password, (2) Email verification, (3) Social login, (4) Profile setup. Each independently deliverable and testable.

Q10: What is the difference between a user story and a use case?

A: User story is brief, user-value focused, with details deferred to conversation. Use case is detailed, step-by-step interaction between actor and system — more formal and comprehensive.

Q11: How do you handle a story with no acceptance criteria?

A: Do not accept into sprint. Flag in refinement; work with PO to define AC before sprint planning. Testing without AC leads to ambiguity disputes and missed defects.

Q12: What is a spike in relation to user stories?

A: Time-boxed research story to answer questions (e.g., "Spike: evaluate payment gateway APIs"). Outcome is knowledge, not shippable feature — informs future stories.

Q13: How does BDD relate to user stories?

A: BDD uses Given-When-Then Gherkin syntax for AC, bridging business language and automated tests. Stories provide context; scenarios provide executable specifications.

Q14: Who writes user stories?

A: Primarily the Product Owner, with input from team. QA contributes testability feedback and AC during refinement — doesn't usually own story authorship.

Q15: How do you estimate a story that is mostly testing effort?

A: Story points cover whole-team effort. If integration testing dominates, vote higher (8 vs 5). Compare to similar past stories. Discuss in Planning Poker — don't estimate in isolation.

Q16: What is story mapping and how does QA use it?

A: Story mapping is a visual technique arranging user activities (backbone) and stories (below) to show user journey and release slices. QA uses it to identify integration test paths across the journey, spot missing edge-case stories, and plan end-to-end test scenarios before sprint commitment.

Q17: How do technical stories differ from user stories?

A: Technical stories (enablers) may use format "As a developer, I want to..." or be written as Tasks. They don't deliver direct user value but enable future stories (e.g., "Set up test data service"). QA validates enablers by verifying downstream stories become testable.

User Story Templates & Variations

TemplateWhen to UseExample
StandardUser-facing featuresAs a customer, I want to track my order, so that I know when it arrives
Job Story (JTBD)Focus on motivation over personaWhen I receive a wrong item, I want to initiate a return quickly, so I can get a refund without calling support
Technical EnablerInfrastructure, refactoringAs a QA engineer, I want a test data factory API, so that tests run with consistent data
Bug Fix StoryDefect requiring sprint capacityAs a user, I want checkout to accept Visa cards, so that I can complete my purchase (regression fix)
NFR StoryNon-functional requirementsAs a user, I want search results in <2 seconds, so that I don't abandon the site

Section 9: Jira Complete Guide

What is Jira?

Jira is Atlassian's issue tracking and project management tool used by Agile teams to plan, track, and release software. It provides boards, backlogs, workflows, dashboards, reporting, and JQL search — making work visible and traceable from idea to production.

Purpose

  • Centralize requirements, bugs, tasks, and test-related work
  • Visualize sprint progress via Scrum/Kanban boards
  • Enforce workflow states (e.g., Ready for QA → Testing → Done)
  • Generate reports: velocity, burndown, cumulative flow
  • Integrate with CI/CD, test management, and collaboration tools

Why Industry Standard

Jira dominates because it is highly configurable (custom workflows, fields, issue types), integrates with the Atlassian ecosystem (Confluence, Bitbucket) and 3000+ marketplace apps (Zephyr, Xray, Jenkins), and scales from startup teams to enterprise SAFe programs. Interview familiarity is expected for Senior QA/SDET roles.

Jira Project Types: Scrum vs Kanban Board

AspectScrum BoardKanban Board
CadenceFixed sprints with start/end datesContinuous flow; no sprints
PlanningSprint Planning selects backlog into sprintPull work when WIP allows
BacklogProduct Backlog + Sprint BacklogSingle prioritized backlog
MetricsVelocity, sprint burndownCycle time, lead time, cumulative flow
WIP LimitsImplicit via sprint commitmentExplicit per column
ReleasesAligned to sprint boundariesRelease anytime
Best For QAFeature teams with planned test cyclesSupport, production bugs, ad-hoc requests
ReportsSprint report, velocity chartControl chart, CFD

Jira Navigation

AreaPurposeQA Use
DashboardPersonalized home with gadgets/widgetsMonitor assigned bugs, sprint progress, filter results
ProjectsContainer for boards, backlog, issuesNavigate to your team's project (e.g., CHECKOUT)
BoardsVisual workflow — Scrum or KanbanTrack stories through Ready for QA → Testing → Done
FiltersSaved JQL queries"My Open Bugs," "Sprint Ready for QA," "Regression Blockers"
ReportsBuilt-in analyticsVelocity, burndown, cumulative flow, sprint report
IssuesGlobal issue search and createQuick bug creation, bulk operations

Issue Types

Issue TypeWhen to CreateDetails
EpicLarge feature spanning multiple sprintsGroups related stories; tracked on roadmap; example: "EPIC-100: Mobile App v2"
StoryUser-facing functionality delivering valueHas story points, AC, sprint assignment; primary QA test target
TaskTechnical/non-user-facing workTest env setup, automation framework upgrade, CI pipeline fix
BugDefect found during testing or productionFields: Summary, Steps to Reproduce, Expected/Actual, Severity, Priority, Environment, Screenshots, Attachments (HAR, logs)
SpikeResearch or investigation time-box"Spike: Evaluate Playwright vs Cypress" — outcome documented in Confluence
SubtaskBreakdown of story or task"Manual test execution," "Write API automation," "Update regression suite"

Bug Fields Explained

  • Summary: Concise title — "Checkout fails when coupon + loyalty points combined"
  • Description: Steps to reproduce, expected vs actual behavior
  • Priority: Business urgency (Highest → Lowest) — set by PO/team
  • Severity: Technical impact (Critical/Major/Minor/Cosmetic) — often set by QA
  • Environment: Staging, Production, Browser/OS version
  • Linked Issues: "Blocks" story, "Relates to" duplicate, "Clones" for retest

Issue Fields

PriorityBusiness urgencyFlag P1 production bugs for immediate attention
LabelsFree-form tagsregression, automation, flaky-test, smoke-test

AssigneePerson responsibleBug assigned to dev; test subtask to QA

JQL (Jira Query Language)

Basic Queries

project = "CHECKOUT"
status = "Ready for QA"
assignee = currentUser()
priority = Highest

Advanced Queries

project = CHECKOUT AND created >= -7d AND labels = regression
component = Payment AND status in ("Testing", "Ready for QA")
fixVersion = "2026-Q3-Release" AND type = Bug AND priority in (Highest, High)

15+ Useful JQL Queries for QA Engineers

#JQL QueryDescription
1project = X AND status = "Ready for QA"All stories awaiting QA pickup
2assignee = currentUser() AND status = TestingMy active test assignments
3type = Bug AND reporter = currentUser() AND created >= -30dBugs I logged last 30 days
4sprint in openSprints() AND status != DoneIncomplete sprint items
5type = Bug AND priority in (Highest, High) AND status != DoneOpen critical/high bugs
6labels = regression AND status = OpenOpen regression failures
7component = Checkout AND type = BugAll checkout module bugs
8fixVersion = "Release-2.5" AND type in (Story, Bug)Release 2.5 scope
9status changed to "Ready for QA" during (-1d, now())Items sent to QA today
10type = Bug AND status = Done AND resolution = Fixed AND updated >= -7dRecently fixed bugs for retest
11parent = STORY-123All subtasks of a story
12"Epic Link" = EPIC-456All stories under an epic
13labels = flaky-test AND status != DoneKnown flaky tests backlog
14type = Story AND "Story Points" > 8Oversized stories needing split
15project = X AND status = Done AND sprint = "Sprint 14"Completed work in Sprint 14
16type = Bug AND created >= startOfMonth() AND reporter in membersOf("qa-team")QA team bugs this month
17summary ~ "payment*" AND type = Bug AND status != DoneOpen payment-related bugs (text search)

Jira Dashboards

Gadgets Useful for QA:

  • Filter Results: Display saved JQL — e.g., "Ready for QA" queue
  • Sprint Burndown: Track remaining work in current sprint
  • Sprint Health: Flags scope creep, at-risk items
  • Pie Chart: Bugs by priority, component, or status
  • Created vs Resolved: Bug trend — are we finding more than fixing?
  • Two-Dimensional Filter Statistics: Matrix of component vs priority
  • Activity Stream: Recent changes on watched issues

Jira Reports

ReportWhat It ShowsQA Value
Velocity ChartStory points completed per sprint over timeCapacity planning; detect if quality debt reduces true velocity
Sprint ReportCommitted vs completed; scope changes mid-sprintReview if untested items were removed or carried over
Burndown ChartRemaining work day-by-day in sprintIdentify if testing is lagging development
Cumulative Flow DiagramIssue count per status over timeBottleneck detection — wide "Testing" band = QA bottleneck
Control ChartCycle time for completed issues (Kanban)How long from In Progress to Done — includes test wait time
Version ReportProgress toward a release versionRelease readiness — open bugs in fix version

Jira Integrations

ToolIntegration PurposeQA Benefit
ConfluenceDocumentation linked to Jira issuesTest plans, AC details, retro notes linked to epics/stories
SlackNotifications on issue changesAlert channel when story moves to Ready for QA or P1 bug logged
Jenkins / GitHub ActionsCI build status on issuesSee if branch builds pass before starting QA; auto-transition on deploy
Zephyr Scale / XrayTest management inside JiraLink test cases to stories; execution results; coverage reports; BDD import
Bitbucket / GitHubBranch/PR linked to issuesTrace code changes to story; smart commits transition status

Best Practices for QA Using Jira

  • Log bugs immediately with complete reproduction steps, screenshots, environment, and severity
  • Link bugs to stories using "blocks" or "relates to" — traceability for release decisions
  • Use subtasks for test work — visible on sprint board, tracked in burndown
  • Apply consistent labels — regression, smoke, automation, flaky — enables powerful JQL filters
  • Transition statuses promptly — don't leave items in "Testing" after completion
  • Comment with test results — "12/12 AC pass, automation PR #445 merged, moving to Done"
  • Create saved filters for daily queues: Ready for QA, My Bugs, Retest Needed
  • Watch critical issues — get notified on status changes without manual checking
  • Don't use Jira as chat — short comments with facts; long discussions in Slack/Confluence with link
  • Keep story points on stories only — not bugs or subtasks (team convention)
  • Review dashboard daily — sprint health, open P1 bugs, items in Testing column
  • Use Zephyr/Xray if available — avoid duplicate test tracking in spreadsheets

Interview Questions & Answers — Jira

Q1: What is Jira and why is it widely used?

A: Atlassian's issue tracking and Agile project management tool. Industry standard due to configurability, Atlassian ecosystem integration, extensive marketplace apps, and support for Scrum, Kanban, and SAFe at scale.

Q2: Difference between Scrum board and Kanban board in Jira?

A: Scrum board uses sprints with sprint backlog and velocity metrics. Kanban board uses continuous flow with WIP limits and cycle time metrics. QA uses Scrum for planned feature work, Kanban for support/production bugs.

Q3: Explain common Jira issue types.

A: Epic (large initiative), Story (user value), Task (technical work), Bug (defect), Spike (research), Subtask (breakdown). QA primarily tests stories, logs bugs, and creates test subtasks.

Q4: What fields are important when logging a bug?

A: Summary, steps to reproduce, expected vs actual, environment (browser/OS/build), severity, priority, screenshots/logs, link to story, assignee.

Q5: What is JQL and give three useful queries for QA.

A: Jira Query Language for searching issues. Examples: status = "Ready for QA", type = Bug AND priority = Highest AND status != Done, sprint in openSprints() AND assignee = currentUser().

Q6: Describe a QA-friendly workflow in Jira.

A: To Do → In Progress → In Review → Ready for QA → Testing → Done. Dev moves to Ready for QA after merge; QA picks up, tests, logs bugs if needed, moves to Done when AC pass.

Q7: What is the difference between Priority and Severity?

A: Severity = technical impact of the bug (Critical to Cosmetic) — usually set by QA. Priority = business urgency for fixing (Highest to Lowest) — usually set by PO/team lead. A cosmetic typo can be Low severity but High priority if on homepage during launch.

Q8: How do you use Jira dashboards as QA?

A: Create personal dashboard with Filter Results (Ready for QA queue), Sprint Burndown, Pie Chart (bugs by priority), and Created vs Resolved trend. Review daily for workload and quality trends.

Q9: What reports help QA identify bottlenecks?

A: Cumulative Flow Diagram — widening "Testing" column indicates QA bottleneck. Burndown — test tasks not decreasing signals falling behind. Sprint Report — scope changes affecting test plan.

Q10: How does Jira integrate with test management tools?

A: Zephyr Scale and Xray are Jira plugins enabling test case creation, linking tests to stories, execution tracking, and coverage reports — all within Jira without separate tools.

Q11: What is a Jira filter and why save them?

A: Saved JQL query reusable for boards, dashboards, and subscriptions. QA saves filters like "Retest Needed," "My Open Bugs," "Sprint Test Queue" for daily efficiency.

Q12: How do you link a bug to a user story in Jira?

A: Use "Link Issue" → "blocks" (bug blocks story completion) or "relates to." Ensures traceability — release decisions consider open blocking bugs on stories.

Q13: What are Components and Labels — when to use each?

A: Components = structured module taxonomy (Checkout, Auth) — one per issue, project-defined. Labels = flexible tags (regression, smoke) — multiple per issue, anyone can add. Both enable JQL filtering.

Q14: How do you track test execution in Jira without Xray/Zephyr?

A: Use subtasks ("Manual test STORY-123"), transition parent story status, comment test results, attach evidence. Less ideal than dedicated test management but workable for small teams.

Q15: What is Fix Version used for?

A: Target release for a bug fix or feature. QA filters fixVersion = "2.5" AND type = Bug AND status != Done to assess release readiness.

Q16: Explain smart commits in Jira.

A: Git commit messages with Jira issue keys trigger automatic actions. Example: git commit -m "CHK-892 Fix tax calculation #done" transitions issue to Done when pushed via Bitbucket/GitHub integration. QA verifies transitions match actual test status — don't auto-close without testing.

Q17: How do you bulk-update issues in Jira?

A: Run a JQL filter → select issues (Bulk Change) → transition, edit fields, or add labels in batch. Useful after regression: label all failed areas regression-sprint-14 or bulk-move verified fixes to Done.

Jira Keyboard Shortcuts & Productivity Tips

ShortcutActionQA Use Case

/Quick searchJump to issue by key: /CHK-892
j / kNavigate issue listMove through filter results without mouse
eEdit selected issueUpdate priority or assignee quickly
assign to meWorkflow commandSelf-assign story from Ready for QA column

Common Jira Mistakes QA Should Avoid

  • Logging bugs without reproduction steps — causes "Cannot Reproduce" churn
  • Leaving resolved bugs unverified — always retest before closing
  • Creating duplicate bugs — search JQL before filing
  • Not linking bugs to parent story — breaks release traceability
  • Using comments for test evidence without attaching logs/screenshots
  • Transitioning to Done when AC partially met — erodes trust in quality gates

Section 10: JIRA Workflow & Project Lifecycle

Understanding Jira end-to-end is essential for Senior QA and SDET roles. Interviewers expect you to explain not just what Jira is, but how requirements flow through the system, how sprints are managed, and how QA fits into every transition.

End-to-End Jira Workflow: Requirement → Epic → Story → Task → Dev → Testing → Release

The Jira project lifecycle mirrors Agile delivery. A business requirement enters as an Epic, gets decomposed into Stories, broken into Tasks and Sub-tasks, developed, tested, and released under a Fix Version.

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    END-TO-END JIRA PROJECT LIFECYCLE                             │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  [Business Requirement]
           │
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     Product Owner creates Epic in Backlog
  │      EPIC       │     Epic: "User Authentication Module"
  │  (Jira Issue)   │     Labels: auth, security | Component: Identity
  └────────┬────────┘
           │ Grooming / Refinement
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     Stories linked to Epic via "Epic Link" or Parent
  │     STORY       │     Story: "As a user, I can register with email"
  │  (User Story)   │     Acceptance Criteria in Description
  └────────┬────────┘
           │ Sprint Planning — team selects stories
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     Dev creates Tasks / Sub-tasks under Story
  │  TASK / SUB-    │     Task: "Implement registration API"
  │     TASK        │     Task: "Create registration UI"
  └────────┬────────┘     Sub-task: "Write unit tests"
           │
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     Developer moves Story: To Do → In Progress → Code Review
  │   DEVELOPMENT   │     Branch linked via Smart Commits or DevOps integration
  └────────┬────────┘
           │
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     QA picks up when Story reaches "Ready for QA" / "In Test"
  │     TESTING     │     Test cases executed, bugs logged and linked
  └────────┬────────┘     Story transitions: In Test → QA Pass / QA Fail
           │
     ┌─────┴─────┐
     ▼           ▼
 [BUGS]     [PASS]
     │           │
     └─────┬─────┘
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐     Story → Done | Fix Version assigned
  │     RELEASE     │     Release notes generated from resolved issues
  └────────┬────────┘     Version deployed: v2.4.0
           ▼
  [Production / Done]

Key Issue Types and Hierarchy

EpicProduct Owner / BALarge feature groupingEpic Name, Start/End Date, Color
StoryPO / BAUser-facing deliverableStory Points, Acceptance Criteria, Sprint
TaskDev / QATechnical work unitAssignee, Original Estimate
BugQA / AnyoneDefect trackingSeverity, Priority, Environment, Steps

Bug Workflow in Jira: Complete Lifecycle

Every organization customizes workflows, but Senior QA candidates should articulate a full bug lifecycle with transitions, assignees, and QA verification gates.

                        BUG LIFECYCLE IN JIRA
                        ═════════════════════

                    ┌─────────────┐
                    │    OPEN     │  ◄── QA creates bug, links to Story
                    │  (Reported) │      Fields: Steps, Expected, Actual,
                    └──────┬──────┘      Environment, Severity, Attachments
                           │
              ┌────────────┼────────────┐
              ▼            ▼            ▼
        ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐
        │ REOPENED │ │ TRIAGED  │ │ REJECTED │──► Invalid / Duplicate / Cannot Reproduce
        │(from Fix)│ │(Triage)  │ │          │
        └────┬─────┘ └────┬─────┘ └──────────┘
             │            │
             └─────┬──────┘
                   ▼
            ┌─────────────┐
            │ IN PROGRESS │  ◄── Auto-assigned to Dev via Component/Module
            │  (Assigned) │
            └──────┬──────┘
                   │
                   ▼
            ┌─────────────┐
            │    FIXED    │  ◄── Dev resolves, adds Fix Version, Root Cause
            │  (Resolved) │
            └──────┬──────┘
                   │
                   ▼
            ┌─────────────┐
            │   VERIFIED  │  ◄── QA retests on QA/Staging environment
            │ (QA Retest) │
            └──────┬──────┘
                   │
          ┌────────┴────────┐
          ▼                 ▼
   ┌─────────────┐   ┌─────────────┐
   │   CLOSED    │   │  REOPENED   │──► Back to IN PROGRESS
   │  (Done)     │   │ (Fail QA)   │
   └─────────────┘   └─────────────┘

Transition Triggers:
  OPEN → IN PROGRESS     : Dev picks up OR automation assigns
  IN PROGRESS → FIXED    : Dev commits fix, updates resolution
  FIXED → VERIFIED       : QA begins retest (auto-notify via automation)
  VERIFIED → CLOSED      : QA confirms fix on target environment
  VERIFIED → REOPENED    : Fix incomplete or regression introduced
  ANY → REJECTED         : PO/Dev marks as not a bug

Essential Bug Fields for QA

FieldWhat to EnterWhy It Matters
SummaryConcise defect titleSearchability in Jira filters
DescriptionSteps to Reproduce, Expected, ActualDev can reproduce without asking QA
EnvironmentQA, Staging, Browser/OSEnvironment-specific bugs
SeverityBlocker/Critical/Major/Minor/TrivialImpact on system
PriorityP1/P2/P3/P4Fix order within sprint
Linked IssuesRelates to / Blocks StoryTraceability to requirement
Fix VersionTarget releaseRelease planning
AttachmentsScreenshots, logs, HAR filesEvidence for triage

Release Management in Jira

Fix Versions

Fix Versions represent planned or completed releases. QA uses them to scope regression, verify release candidates, and confirm which bugs ship in which release.

Workflow: Create version (v2.4.0) → Assign to Stories/Bugs during development → Mark "Released" on deploy day → Archive old versions.
QA responsibility: Filter fixVersion = "v2.4.0" AND status != Done before sign-off to ensure nothing slips through.

Release Notes Generation

Jira can auto-generate release notes from resolved issues grouped by type (New Features, Bug Fixes, Known Issues). QA validates accuracy — especially bug fix descriptions visible to customers.

Release Note SectionJira JQL FilterQA Action
New Featurestype = Story AND fixVersion = v2.4.0Verify feature list matches demo
Bug Fixestype = Bug AND fixVersion = v2.4.0 AND status = ClosedConfirm customer-facing wording
Known Issuestype = Bug AND fixVersion = v2.4.0 AND status != ClosedDocument workarounds

Jira Automation Rules Useful for QA

1. Auto-Assign Bugs to Dev When Status Changes

Rule: When Bug transitions to "In Progress"
Trigger: Issue transitioned → In Progress
Condition: Issue type = Bug
Action: Assign issue to user in custom field "Module Owner"
        OR assign based on Component (Auth → dev-auth-team lead)

2. Auto-Transition When Subtasks Complete

Rule: Move Story to "Ready for QA" when all sub-tasks done
Trigger: Sub-task transitioned → Done
Condition: All sub-tasks of parent Story are Done
           AND parent status = "In Progress"
Action: Transition parent Story → "Ready for QA"
        Add comment: "All development sub-tasks complete. Ready for QA."

3. Notification Rules

RuleTriggerNotify
Bug CreatedIssue created, type = BugDev lead, PO (if Blocker)
Bug FixedStatus → FixedQA reporter via @mention
Story Ready for QAStatus → Ready for QAQA assignee, Slack channel
Sprint StartedSprint activatedEntire team
Release DeployedFix Version releasedQA for smoke test trigger

Board Configuration

Columns and Workflow Mapping

ColumnMapped StatusesWIP LimitPurpose
To DoOpen, BacklogNoneSprint backlog items
In ProgressIn Progress, In Development4Limit concurrent dev work
Code ReviewIn Review, PR Open3Prevent review bottleneck
In TestReady for QA, In Test3QA capacity management
DoneDone, ClosedNoneCompleted work

Swimlanes

Common swimlane strategies: by Epic (feature visibility), by Assignee (individual workload), by Priority (P1 bugs surfaced first). QA boards often use swimlanes by Epic during regression to track feature completion.

Sprint Planning in Jira

Capacity Planning

Formula: Team Capacity = (Team Members × Available Days × Hours/Day) − Meetings − PTO
Example: 5 devs + 2 QA × 10 days × 6 productive hours = 420 hours − 40 hours ceremonies = 380 hours
Velocity: Use average of last 3 sprints (e.g., 42 points) — do not over-commit.

Story Selection Process

  1. PO presents prioritized backlog filtered by Epic/Roadmap
  2. Team reviews Story Points, dependencies, and Definition of Ready
  3. Stories dragged into Sprint — total points ≤ velocity
  4. Tasks created and estimated in hours
  5. Sprint Goal documented in Jira Sprint field

Sprint Closure Process

StepAction in JiraOwner
1. Complete testingAll stories Done or moved to next sprintQA
2. Close verified bugsBugs in Verified → ClosedQA
3. Move incomplete workDrag unfinished stories back to backlogPO
4. Update Fix VersionsConfirm version assignment on all Done itemsDev Lead
5. Generate sprint reportSprint Report → Burndown, VelocityScrum Master
6. Close sprintComplete Sprint in Jira — auto-moves open itemsScrum Master
7. RetrospectiveDocument action items as Tasks for next sprintTeam

Interview Questions & Answers (Section 10)

Q1: Explain the Jira issue hierarchy from Epic to Sub-task.

A: Epic is the largest container for a feature initiative. Stories (or User Stories) deliver user value and link to Epics. Tasks break stories into dev/QA work. Sub-tasks are the smallest units assigned to individuals. Bugs can link to Stories independently. In Jira Cloud, Epics can also be parents in next-gen projects.

Q2: What is the difference between Priority and Severity in Jira bugs?

A: Severity measures technical impact (Blocker = system down). Priority measures business urgency for fix order (P1 = fix immediately). A cosmetic UI bug might be Low Severity but High Priority if a key client demo is tomorrow.

Q3: How do you use Fix Versions in release management?

A: Fix Version tags which release includes a fix or feature. Before release, I run JQL to find open issues in that version. After deployment, I mark the version Released and generate release notes from resolved issues.

Q4: Describe a Jira workflow you configured or improved for QA.

A: I added a "Ready for QA" status between Code Review and In Test. Automation notifies QA on transition. Stories cannot move to Done without passing through Verified. This prevents devs from closing stories before QA sign-off.

Q5: What JQL query finds all open bugs blocking a release?

A: project = PROJ AND type = Bug AND fixVersion = "v2.4.0" AND status not in (Closed, Done, Rejected). Add AND priority in (P1, P2) for critical blockers only.

Q6: How do WIP limits help QA teams?

A: WIP limits on "In Test" column (e.g., 3) prevent dev from flooding QA with stories. When limit is reached, team swarms on testing before pulling new dev work — improving flow and reducing context switching.

Q7: Explain sprint velocity and how it guides planning.

A: Velocity is completed story points per sprint, averaged over 3+ sprints. If average is 40 points, we commit ~40 points next sprint. It's a planning guide, not a performance metric — teams shouldn't inflate estimates to increase velocity.

Q8: What happens to incomplete stories when a sprint closes?

A: Jira moves them back to the backlog (or next sprint if manually moved). Their story points don't count toward velocity. Sprint Report shows spillover — a signal for retrospective discussion on over-commitment or blockers.

Q9: How do you link a bug to the story it was found in?

A: Use "Linked Issues" → "relates to" or "is caused by" the Story. Also set the Epic Link to maintain traceability. Some teams use "Blocks" if the bug prevents story completion.

Q10: What automation would you set up for bug triage?

A: When Bug is created with Severity = Blocker, auto-assign to on-call dev, notify PO via Slack, and add label "needs-triage". When status stays Open > 24 hours, escalate to dev lead with email notification.

Q11: Difference between Scrum board and Kanban board in Jira?

A: Scrum boards are tied to Sprints with start/end dates and backlog grooming. Kanban boards are continuous flow without sprints, ideal for support/ops teams. Both support columns, WIP limits, and swimlanes.

Q12: How do Smart Commits integrate Git with Jira?

A: Commit messages like PROJ-123 #comment Fixed login #time 2h #resolve automatically update Jira issues — adding comments, logging time, and transitioning status. QA verifies these transitions match actual test results.

Section 11: JIRA for QA Engineers

Jira is the operational hub for QA in Agile teams. Senior QA and SDET candidates must demonstrate daily Jira fluency — from sprint planning through metrics reporting — not just bug logging.

QA Daily Activities in Jira: Day-by-Day Sprint Breakdown

A typical 2-week (10 working day) sprint from a QA engineer's perspective:

Days 1–2: Sprint Planning, Story Analysis, Test Case Creation

DayActivityJira ActionsDeliverables

"@PO — AC #3 says OTP expires in 5 minutes. Is resend OTP allowed before expiry? What is max resend count? @Dev — Is OTP stored hashed in DB? Need test data setup for expired OTP scenario."

  • Day 9: Full sprint regression on QA staging. Verify Fix Version assignments. Move passed stories to Done. Document known issues for demo.

PMRetrospectiveCreate improvement Tasks (e.g., "Add OTP test data script") for next sprint

Requirement Analysis Using Jira

How to Read Stories Effectively

  1. Summary + Description: User role, action, and benefit (As a / I want / So that)
  2. Acceptance Criteria: Testable conditions — each AC becomes ≥1 test case
  3. Attachments: Mockups, API specs, data models
  4. Linked Issues: Dependencies, blocked-by stories, related bugs
  5. Custom Fields: Platform, API endpoint, Feature flag name

Asking Questions in Comments

Best practices: Tag relevant people (@PO, @Dev). Reference specific AC numbers. Propose edge cases. Convert agreed answers into story updates or AC amendments. Use "Questions" label until resolved.

Test Planning in Jira

Linking Test Cases to Stories

Xray Test SetCreate Test issue; link to Story via "Tests" associationFull traceability, execution tracking
Zephyr ScaleTest Case linked via traceability tab on StoryEnterprise test management
Sub-task"QA: Execute registration tests" sub-task under StorySimple teams without test plugin
Confluence linkTest plan page URL in Story descriptionDocumentation-heavy teams

Using Labels and Components

Label/ComponentUsageExample Filter
regressionTests in regression suitelabels = regression AND sprint = current

automationAutomated test coveragelabels = automation AND status = Done

QA Best Practices in Jira (12 Tips)

  1. Always link bugs to the story where they were found — never orphan bugs
  2. Use consistent Severity/Priority definitions documented in Confluence
  3. Include build number and environment in every bug — saves retest cycles
  4. Log time on test tasks for capacity planning accuracy
  5. Comment on stories when testing starts and completes — visibility for team
  6. Use templates for bug descriptions (Steps/Expected/Actual)
  7. Apply labels consistently: regression, smoke, automation, prod-bug
  8. Review "Ready for QA" queue daily — don't let stories sit untested
  9. Verify Fix Version before closing bugs — prevents wrong release attribution
  10. Export sprint metrics before sprint close — historical data for trends
  11. Use @mentions sparingly but effectively — tag dev for blockers only
  12. Keep dashboards updated — stale gadgets erode team trust in QA reporting

Common Mistakes QA Makes in Jira

MistakeImpactCorrect Approach
Vague bug summaries ("Login broken")Dev cannot prioritize or reproduceSpecific: "[Login] SSO redirect fails on Safari 17"
Not linking bugs to storiesLost traceability; PO can't assess story qualityAlways use Linked Issues → relates to Story
Closing bugs without retestingDefect leakage to productionVerify on same environment class where found
Creating duplicate bugsNoise in backlog; wasted dev timeSearch before creating; link as duplicate if exists
Ignoring story commentsTest wrong behavior; AC misunderstandingsRead all comments; ask questions Day 1-2
Not updating test execution statusFalse progress reportingUpdate Xray/Zephyr in real-time during execution
Setting wrong Fix VersionRelease scope errorsConfirm with dev lead before bug creation

Interview Questions & Answers (Section 11)

Q1: Walk me through your typical day as QA using Jira.

A: I start by checking my "Ready for QA" filter and open bugs needing retest. I update the sprint board, execute tests linked to in-progress stories, log defects with full reproduction steps, and comment on stories with test progress. End of day I update test execution reports and flag blockers in standup.

Q2: How do you ensure test coverage is traceable to requirements in Jira?

A: Each acceptance criterion maps to one or more test cases linked via Xray/Zephyr. I generate a traceability matrix report showing Story → Test Cases → Execution Result → Defects. Gaps (AC with no linked test) are flagged before testing starts.

Q3: How do you calculate and report defect density?

A: Defect Density = Total bugs found in sprint / Story points completed. If Sprint 12 had 8 bugs and 40 points, density = 0.2. I track trend over sprints — increasing density signals quality issues in new features or tech debt.

Q4: What JQL do you use daily as QA?

A: Key queries: (1) status = "Ready for QA" AND sprint in openSprints(), (2) type = Bug AND status = Fixed AND reporter = currentUser(), (3) sprint in openSprints() AND assignee = currentUser() AND status != Done.

Q5: How do you handle a bug that cannot be reproduced?

A: Add detailed logs, video recording, HAR file. Tag "intermittent" label. If dev cannot reproduce, move to Cannot Reproduce with comment documenting attempts. Reopen if seen again with additional evidence. Never close without team agreement.

Q6: Compare Zephyr Scale vs Xray for Jira test management.

A: Both are native Jira apps. Xray uses Jira issue types (Test, Test Plan) — good for teams wanting everything as Jira issues. Zephyr Scale has a dedicated test repository with versioning — better for large enterprise test libraries. Both support traceability and CI integration; choice depends on team size and BDD needs.

Q7: How do you track defect leakage in Jira?

A: Production bugs get label "prod-bug" and Component matching the feature. Leakage Rate = prod-bugs / (QA bugs + prod-bugs) × 100. Root cause analysis on each prod bug: missed AC, missing test case, environment gap, or regression.

Q8: What should a good bug report contain?

A: Clear summary, numbered reproduction steps, expected vs actual result, environment details (OS, browser, build), test data used, screenshots/logs attached, severity/priority, linked story, and Fix Version. A developer should reproduce without asking me questions.

Q9: How do you use Jira dashboards to communicate QA status?

A: My dashboard shows: open bugs by priority (pie), test execution progress (bar), bugs created vs resolved trend (line), and stories in "In Test" (filter results). I share the dashboard link in sprint reviews instead of building slides manually.

Q10: How do you manage test cases for regression in Jira?

A: Tag regression test cases with label "regression" and organize into a Test Set/Cycle per release. Each sprint, clone the cycle, execute against the staging build, and track pass/fail. Failed tests either log new bugs or reopen existing ones.

Q11: What is your approach to requirement clarification in Jira?

A: During Days 1-2, I review every story's AC and post structured questions as comments. I identify edge cases (empty input, max length, concurrent users) and propose additional AC if missing. I don't start test case writing until critical questions are resolved.

Q12: How do you prevent duplicate bug reports?

A: Before creating a bug, I search JQL: text ~ "OTP expired" AND project = PROJ AND status != Closed. If found, I add a comment with my additional evidence and link as "duplicates" rather than creating a new issue.

Section 12: Agile Testing

Agile Testing is not a phase — it is continuous quality feedback integrated into every sprint activity. Senior QA and SDET interviews heavily test your understanding of testing quadrants, shift-left/right, CI/CD gates, and automation strategy.

What is Agile Testing?

Agile Testing applies testing principles within Agile development: short iterations, continuous feedback, whole-team quality ownership, and adapting test activities to changing requirements. Unlike Waterfall (test after build), Agile embeds testing from story refinement through production monitoring.

Core Principles: Test early and often | Whole team owns quality | Face-to-face communication | Respond to change | Working software over documentation | Continuous improvement each retrospective

Agile Testing Quadrants (Brian Marick's Model)

QuadrantOrientationAudienceTest TypesAutomationExamples
Q1Technology-facing, supporting teamDevelopersUnit, ComponentHighly automatedJUnit tests, API unit tests, TDD
Q2Business-facing, supporting teamDevelopers, QAFunctional, Story, PrototypeAutomated + ManualSelenium story tests, Cucumber scenarios
Q3Business-facing, critiquing productBusiness, QAExploratory, UAT, Alpha/BetaMostly manualExploratory sessions, usability testing

  Sprint Timeline Mapping:
    Refinement → Q2 (story test design), Q3 (exploratory ideas)
    Development → Q1 (unit), Q2 (automated functional)
    Testing     → Q2 (execution), Q3 (exploratory), Q4 (NFR)
    Release     → Q4 (perf/security gate), Q3 (UAT sign-off)

Shift Left Testing

Concept and Benefits

Shift Left moves testing activities earlier in the development lifecycle — during requirements, design, and coding — rather than waiting for a completed build.

BenefitImpact
Early defect detectionBugs found in design cost 10× less than in production
Faster feedbackDevs fix issues while context is fresh
Better requirementsQA questions expose ambiguities before coding
Reduced reworkFewer sprint spillovers due to late-found bugs

How QA Implements Shift Left

  • Participate in backlog refinement — review AC before sprint planning
  • Write test cases during development, not after
  • Pair with developers on testable code design
  • Run API tests against dev environment before UI is ready
  • Review pull requests for test coverage and edge cases
  • Set up pre-commit hooks running smoke tests locally

Real Example: Registration Feature

Without Shift Left: Dev completes US-201 → QA tests Day 8 → finds OTP expiry bug → fix takes 2 days → story spills.
With Shift Left: QA reviews AC Day 1 → asks "What is OTP expiry?" → PO clarifies 5 min → QA writes API test Day 3 against dev branch → bug found Day 4 → dev fixes same day → UI testing Day 7 proceeds smoothly.

Shift Right Testing

Shift Right extends testing into production and post-release monitoring — complementing Shift Left, not replacing it.

PracticeDescriptionTools
Production monitoringTrack error rates, latency, user flowsDatadog, New Relic, Sentry
Canary releasesDeploy to 5% traffic; monitor before full rolloutFeature flags, Kubernetes
A/B testingCompare feature variants with real usersLaunchDarkly, Optimizely
Chaos engineeringInject failures to test resilienceChaos Monkey, Gremlin
Synthetic monitoringAutomated probes simulating user journeysPingdom, Checkly

QA Gates at Each Stage

StageGate CriteriaFailure Action
Unit Tests≥ 80% code coverage; 0 failuresBlock merge to main
Integration TestsAll API contract tests passBlock deploy to QA
Functional TestsSmoke 100% pass; regression ≥ 95%Block release candidate
Performance TestsResponse p95 < SLA; error rate < 0.1%Block production deploy
Security ScanZero critical/high vulnerabilitiesBlock deploy; create Jira security bug

Test Automation in Agile

What to Automate vs What NOT to Automate

CriteriaAutomate ✅Do NOT Automate ❌
FrequencyRuns every sprint/build (regression, smoke)One-time ad hoc checks
StabilityStable UI/API with defined assertionsFlaky, frequently changing UI
DataDeterministic test data availableComplex visual/layout validation
ROIHigh execution count justifies maintenanceLow-value edge case run once
TypeAPI tests, CRUD flows, data-driven testsExploratory, usability, one-off investigations
Speed needMust run in CI within minutesTests requiring manual judgment

Test Pyramid

                    TEST AUTOMATION PYRAMID
                    ═══════════════════════

                         ┌───────┐
                         │  E2E  │  ← Few (5-10%): Slow, brittle, expensive
                         │  UI   │     Selenium, Playwright, Cypress
                       ┌─┴───────┴─┐
                       │Integration│  ← Some (20-30%): API, DB, service tests
                       │   Tests   │     REST Assured, Postman, Testcontainers
                     ┌─┴───────────┴─┐
                     │   Unit Tests   │  ← Many (60-70%): Fast, cheap, stable
                     │   (Dev-owned)  │     JUnit, TestNG, pytest
                     └───────────────┘

  Rule: If E2E test fails, ask "Could this be caught at integration or unit level?"

Automation ROI Calculation

ROI = (Manual Execution Cost × Runs per Year − Automation Maintenance Cost) / Automation Investment

Example: Regression suite = 40 manual hours × $50/hr = $2,000 per run × 26 sprints = $52,000/year manual cost.
Automation investment = 200 hours × $50 = $10,000. Maintenance = 40 hours/year × $50 = $2,000/year.
Automated run cost = 2 hours × $50 × 26 = $2,600/year.
ROI = ($52,000 − $2,600 − $2,000) / $10,000 = 4.74× return in Year 1.

Testing in Each Sprint Phase

PhaseTesting ActivityTools
Sprint PlanningReview AC, identify testability gaps, estimate QA effortJira, Confluence
RefinementWrite test scenarios, clarify requirements, define test data needsJira comments, Miro
Development (Days 1-5)API testing on dev builds, unit test review, test case authoringREST Assured, Postman, Git
Development (Days 5-8)Functional testing, bug logging, automation script updatesSelenium/Playwright, Jira
Testing (Days 7-9)Full story testing, regression, cross-browser, retesting fixesTestNG, BrowserStack, Xray
Sprint End (Day 10)Regression sign-off, sprint demo support, test reportAllure, Jira Dashboard
ReleaseSmoke on staging, performance gate, production verificationJenkins, JMeter, Datadog

BDD (Behavior Driven Development)

Gherkin Syntax

Feature: User Registration
  As a new visitor
  I want to register with my email
  So that I can access the platform

  Background:
    Given the registration page is open

  Scenario: Successful email registration
    When I enter email "user@test.com"
    And I enter password "SecurePass1!"
    And I click the Register button
    Then I should see "Verify your email"
    And a verification email should be sent to "user@test.com"

  Scenario Outline: Invalid password rejected
    When I enter email "user@test.com"
    And I enter password "<password>"
    And I click the Register button
    Then I should see error "<error_message>"

    Examples:
      | password   | error_message                    |
      | short      | Password must be at least 8 chars|
      | nodigits   | Password must contain a number   |
      | noSpecial  | Password must contain a special  |

Cucumber Integration

Feature files (.feature) live in src/test/resources/features/. Step definitions in Java map Gherkin steps to Selenium/API code. Cucumber hooks handle setup/teardown. Reports integrate with Allure for stakeholder-readable output.

TDD vs BDD vs ATDD Comparison

AspectTDDBDDATDD
Full FormTest-Driven DevelopmentBehavior-Driven DevelopmentAcceptance Test-Driven Development
Primary OwnerDeveloperWhole team (3 Amigos)QA + PO + Dev
LanguageCode (JUnit, TestNG)Gherkin (Given/When/Then)Acceptance criteria → automated tests
FocusCode design via unit testsBehavior specificationAcceptance criteria validation
Test LevelUnit testsFunctional/E2EAcceptance/Story level
When AppliedDuring codingDuring refinement + codingBefore/during sprint start
ToolsJUnit, NUnit, pytestCucumber, SpecFlow, BehaveRobot Framework, FitNesse, Cucumber
AudienceDevelopersBusiness + Dev + QAPO + QA + Dev

Definition of Done for Testing

Testing DoD Checklist (team-agreed):
  • All acceptance criteria verified with evidence
  • Unit test coverage ≥ 80% for new code
  • Automated functional tests pass in CI
  • No open P1/P2 bugs on the story
  • Test cases linked and executed in test management tool
  • Regression suite pass rate ≥ 95%
  • Cross-browser testing complete (Chrome, Firefox, Safari)
  • API tests pass against staging environment
  • Performance baseline met (if applicable)
  • Test data cleaned up; no orphaned records

Interview Questions & Answers (Section 12)

Q1: What is Agile Testing and how is it different from traditional testing?

A: Agile Testing is continuous and iterative — testing happens throughout the sprint alongside development, not as a separate phase after coding. Testers collaborate daily with dev and PO, adapt to changing requirements, and automate regression to keep pace with frequent releases.

Q2: Explain the four Agile Testing Quadrants.

A: Q1 (unit/component, tech, support team), Q2 (functional/story, business, support team), Q3 (exploratory/UAT, business, critique product), Q4 (performance/security, tech, critique product). All four quadrants are needed — not just Q2 functional testing.

Q3: What is Shift Left testing? Give a practical example.

A: Shift Left means testing earlier in the lifecycle. Example: During refinement, I review acceptance criteria and identify that "password must be strong" is vague. I ask PO to define rules before dev starts. I write API tests against the dev branch on Day 3 — finding a validation bug before UI is even built.

Q4: What is Shift Right testing?

A: Shift Right extends testing into production — monitoring real user behavior, canary deployments, feature flags, synthetic monitoring, and chaos engineering. It catches issues that lab environments miss: real traffic patterns, data edge cases, and infrastructure failures.

Q5: Describe QA gates in a CI/CD pipeline.

A: Each pipeline stage has pass/fail criteria that block progression. Unit tests must pass with ≥80% coverage before merge. Integration tests gate deploy to QA. Functional smoke/regression gates release candidate. Performance and security scans gate production deploy. Failures notify QA and dev via Slack/Jira.

Q6: Explain the Test Automation Pyramid.

A: Base = many fast unit tests (60-70%). Middle = integration/API tests (20-30%). Top = few E2E UI tests (5-10%). The pyramid shape reflects speed, stability, and cost — push tests as low as possible. E2E tests are slow and brittle; rely on them sparingly.

Q7: What tests should you NOT automate?

A: Exploratory tests, one-time investigations, frequently changing UI features, tests requiring human judgment (usability, visual design), unstable/flaky scenarios, and tests where automation maintenance exceeds manual execution cost.

Q8: How do you calculate automation ROI?

A: ROI = (Manual cost per year − Automated run cost − Maintenance cost) / Initial investment. If manual regression costs $52K/year and automation costs $10K to build + $4.6K/year to run/maintain, ROI = 3.4× in Year 1. Present this to justify automation sprint capacity.

Q9: What is BDD and how does Gherkin help?

A: BDD uses natural language (Gherkin: Given/When/Then) to define behavior collaboratively with PO, dev, and QA. Feature files become living documentation and automated test scripts via Cucumber step definitions. It bridges communication gaps between technical and business teams.

Q10: Compare TDD, BDD, and ATDD.

A: TDD is developer-driven unit testing before code (Red-Green-Refactor). BDD specifies behavior in Gherkin for the whole team. ATDD defines acceptance tests from AC before development starts — typically in "Three Amigos" sessions. They complement each other: TDD for code quality, ATDD for requirements, BDD for communication.

Q11: What is your Definition of Done for testing?

A: All AC verified, automated tests pass in CI, no open P1/P2 bugs, test cases executed and linked in Xray, regression ≥95% pass, cross-browser tested, and test data cleaned up. DoD is team-agreed and displayed in Confluence — not QA-only criteria.

Q12: How do you balance manual and automated testing in a sprint?

A: Automate regression and smoke tests for stable features. Manual effort focuses on new story testing (first-time validation), exploratory testing (Q3), and complex scenarios hard to automate. Each sprint I allocate ~60% execution on automation, ~40% on manual/exploratory for new features.

Q13: How does continuous testing differ from test automation?

A: Test automation is writing scripts to execute tests. Continuous testing is the practice of running the right tests automatically at every pipeline stage with quality gates. It includes automation plus CI integration, test selection, environment management, and result-driven deploy decisions.

Q14: What testing activities happen during backlog refinement?

A: QA reviews stories for testability, identifies missing AC, proposes edge cases, estimates testing effort, and flags dependencies. I ask: "How do we test this? What test data is needed? Are there NFR requirements?" This is Shift Left in action.

Q15: How do you handle testing when requirements change mid-sprint?

A: Assess impact on existing test cases and automation scripts. Update test cases in Jira/Xray. Communicate scope change to SM/PO. Reprioritize — drop lower-priority tests if needed. Update AC comments with agreed changes. Never silently test against old requirements.

Q16: What role does QA play in CI/CD?

A: QA defines quality gates, maintains automated test suites in the pipeline, triages test failures (bug vs flaky test), manages test environments and data, reviews deployment checklists, and performs smoke tests post-deploy. QA is a pipeline stakeholder, not just a consumer of builds.

Section 13: Real-Time Project Scenarios

Interviewers for Senior QA and SDET roles often present live scenarios: "Here's a user story — how would you test it?" This section provides five end-to-end scenarios with requirements, stories, test cases, SQL validation, sample defects, and Jira workflow walkthroughs.

Scenario 1: Login Feature Testing

Requirement

The application must support secure user authentication via multiple methods (email, phone, SSO), with session management (Remember Me), password recovery, and account lockout after repeated failed attempts.

User Story with Acceptance Criteria

US-501: User Login
As a registered user, I want to log in using email, phone, or SSO, so that I can access my account securely.

Acceptance Criteria:
  1. User can log in with valid email + password → redirected to dashboard
  2. User can log in with valid phone number + OTP → redirected to dashboard
  3. User can log in via Google SSO → account linked or created
  4. "Remember Me" keeps session active for 30 days on trusted device
  5. "Forgot Password" sends reset link valid for 15 minutes
  6. Account locks after 5 consecutive failed password attempts for 30 minutes
  7. Invalid credentials show generic error: "Invalid email or password" (no user enumeration)
  8. Session expires after 24 hours of inactivity (without Remember Me)

Test Cases

TC IDTest CasePreconditionStepsExpected ResultPriority
TC-L01Valid email loginUser exists: john@test.comEnter email + valid password → LoginRedirect to /dashboard; session createdP1
TC-L02Valid phone + OTP loginUser with phone +91-9876543210Enter phone → Request OTP → Enter OTP → LoginRedirect to dashboardP1
TC-L03Google SSO loginGoogle account linkedClick "Sign in with Google" → AuthorizeRedirect to dashboard; SSO token storedP1
TC-L04Remember Me — 30 day sessionValid userCheck Remember Me → Login → Close browser → Reopen after 1 dayUser still logged inP2
TC-L05Forgot Password flowRegistered emailClick Forgot Password → Enter email → Check inbox → Click reset link → Set new passwordPassword updated; can login with new passwordP1
TC-L06Account lockout after 5 failuresValid user accountEnter wrong password 5 timesAccount locked message; login blocked for 30 minP1
TC-L07Invalid credentials — no enumerationNoneLogin with non-existent email OR wrong passwordSame error: "Invalid email or password"P1
TC-L08Session timeout — 24hr inactivityLogged in without Remember MeWait 24+ hours idle → perform actionRedirect to login pageP2
TC-L09Expired reset linkReset link generatedWait 16 minutes → click reset linkError: "Link expired. Request a new one."P2
TC-L10SSO — new user auto-registrationGoogle account NOT linkedSign in with Google (first time)Account created; redirected to profile setupP2

SQL Validation Queries

-- Verify successful login creates session record
SELECT u.email, s.session_token, s.expires_at, s.remember_me
FROM users u
JOIN user_sessions s ON u.id = s.user_id
WHERE u.email = 'john@test.com'
  AND s.is_active = 1
ORDER BY s.created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;

-- Verify account lockout after 5 failed attempts
SELECT email, failed_login_count, locked_until, status
FROM users
WHERE email = 'john@test.com';
-- Expected: failed_login_count = 5, locked_until = NOW() + 30 min, status = 'LOCKED'

-- Verify password reset token expiry
SELECT email, reset_token, reset_token_expires_at
FROM users
WHERE email = 'john@test.com';
-- Expected: reset_token_expires_at within 15 minutes of created_at

Defects Found (Sample)

Bug IDSummarySeverityRoot Cause
BUG-601Account lockout triggers after 3 attempts, not 5MajorConfig value wrong in auth-service.properties
BUG-602Non-existent email shows "User not found" — enumeration riskCriticalDifferent error messages in AuthController
BUG-603Remember Me session expires after 7 days, not 30MinorCookie maxAge set to 604800 instead of 2592000

Scenario 2: Order Placement Flow (E-Commerce)

Requirement

Registered users must be able to add products to cart, proceed through checkout with address and payment details, apply discount codes, and receive order confirmation. System must validate stock availability and calculate prices correctly including taxes and discounts.

User Story with Acceptance Criteria

US-601: Place Order
As a registered user, I want to complete an order from cart to confirmation, so that I receive my purchased products.

Acceptance Criteria:
  1. User can add products to cart and view updated cart total
  2. Checkout validates stock availability before order creation
  3. User selects/adds shipping address during checkout
  4. Price = (Unit Price × Quantity) − Discount + Tax (18% GST)
  5. Valid discount code reduces total; invalid/expired code shows error
  6. Payment success → order status = CONFIRMED, confirmation email sent
  7. Order confirmation page shows order ID, items, total, estimated delivery
  8. Out-of-stock item cannot be checked out — user notified to remove item

SQL Validation Queries

-- Verify order created with correct totals after checkout
SELECT o.order_id, o.status, o.subtotal, o.discount_amount,
       o.tax_amount, o.total_amount, oi.product_id, oi.quantity, oi.unit_price
FROM orders o
JOIN order_items oi ON o.order_id = oi.order_id
WHERE o.user_id = (SELECT id FROM users WHERE email = 'buyer@test.com')
ORDER BY o.created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;
-- Expected: status='CONFIRMED', total = subtotal - discount + tax

-- Verify stock decremented after order
SELECT p.sku, p.stock_quantity, p.reserved_quantity
FROM products p
WHERE p.sku = 'SKU-101';
-- Expected: stock_quantity decreased by ordered qty

-- Verify discount code usage tracked
SELECT dc.code, dc.times_used, dc.max_uses, ou.order_id
FROM discount_codes dc
JOIN order_discounts od ON dc.id = od.discount_code_id
JOIN orders ou ON od.order_id = ou.order_id
WHERE dc.code = 'SAVE10'
ORDER BY ou.created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;

Scenario 3: Payment Integration Testing

Requirement

Integrate payment gateway supporting credit card, debit card, UPI, and wallet payments. Handle success, failure, timeout, and refund scenarios. Comply with PCI DSS — no card data stored in application database.

User Story with Acceptance Criteria

US-701: Payment Processing
As a customer, I want to pay using my preferred payment method, so that I can complete my purchase securely.

Acceptance Criteria:
  1. Credit/debit card payment via gateway → order status = PAID on success
  2. UPI payment with valid VPA → payment confirmed within 60 seconds
  3. Wallet payment deducts balance and confirms order
  4. Failed payment (declined card) → order status = PAYMENT_FAILED; user can retry
  5. Payment timeout (no response in 120s) → order status = PAYMENT_PENDING; retry allowed
  6. Refund initiated → amount credited within 5-7 business days; order status = REFUNDED
  7. No raw card numbers stored in DB — only tokenized reference (PCI DSS)
  8. Payment amount must match order total exactly — mismatch rejected

PCI DSS Brief

PCI DSS Requirements for QA: Never log full card numbers in test evidence. Use gateway test cards only (e.g., 4111111111111111). Verify application stores only payment_token, last4, card_brand — never CVV or full PAN. Test that API responses don't expose card data. Verify HTTPS on all payment endpoints.

Test Cases

TC IDTest CasePreconditionStepsExpected ResultPriority
TC-P01Credit card — successful paymentOrder ₹1180, test card 4111...1111Select Card → Enter details → PayPayment success; order = PAID; receipt shownP1
TC-P02Debit card — successful paymentOrder ₹500, test debit cardSelect Debit Card → PayPayment success; order = PAIDP1
TC-P03UPI payment — successOrder ₹2000, valid VPA test@upiSelect UPI → Enter VPA → Confirm on UPI appPayment confirmed within 60s; order = PAIDP1
TC-P04Wallet payment — sufficient balanceWallet balance ₹5000, order ₹1500Select Wallet → PayBalance deducted to ₹3500; order = PAIDP1
TC-P05Declined card — payment failureTest card 4000...0002 (decline)Enter declined card → PayError: "Payment declined"; order = PAYMENT_FAILED; retry option shownP1
TC-P06Payment timeoutSimulate gateway delay >120sInitiate payment → wait 120sStatus = PAYMENT_PENDING; "Retry Payment" button shownP2
TC-P07Refund — full refundOrder PAID ₹1180Admin initiates refundOrder = REFUNDED; refund record created; customer notifiedP1
TC-P08Amount mismatch rejectedOrder total ₹1180Intercept API; send amount ₹1000Payment rejected; error logged; order unchangedP1
TC-P09Wallet — insufficient balanceWallet balance ₹100, order ₹500Select Wallet → PayError: "Insufficient wallet balance"P2
TC-P10PCI — no card data in DBSuccessful card paymentQuery payments table for card numberOnly payment_token, last4, brand stored; no PAN/CVVP1

SQL Validation Queries

-- Verify payment record after successful transaction
SELECT p.payment_id, p.order_id, p.method, p.amount, p.status,
       p.gateway_transaction_id, p.payment_token, p.card_last4
FROM payments p
JOIN orders o ON p.order_id = o.order_id
WHERE o.order_id = 'ORD-2024-00142'
ORDER BY p.created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;
-- Expected: status='SUCCESS', amount=1180.00, payment_token NOT NULL, card_last4='1111'

-- Verify NO sensitive card data stored (PCI DSS)
SELECT column_name FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name = 'payments'
  AND column_name IN ('card_number', 'cvv', 'pan');
-- Expected: 0 rows (these columns must NOT exist)

-- Verify refund record
SELECT r.refund_id, r.payment_id, r.amount, r.status, r.initiated_at
FROM refunds r
WHERE r.payment_id = (SELECT payment_id FROM payments WHERE order_id = 'ORD-2024-00142')
ORDER BY r.created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;
-- Expected: status='INITIATED' or 'COMPLETED', amount matches original payment

Scenario 4: User Registration

Requirement

New users register with email or phone, verify identity via OTP, and set a strong password. System prevents duplicate registrations and validates all form inputs server-side and client-side.

User Story with Acceptance Criteria

US-801: User Registration
As a new visitor, I want to create an account with email or phone, so that I can access platform features.

Acceptance Criteria:
  1. Valid email + strong password + OTP verification → account created
  2. Valid phone + OTP verification → account created with phone as identifier
  3. Password: min 8 chars, 1 uppercase, 1 lowercase, 1 number, 1 special character
  4. Duplicate email registration blocked with error "Email already registered"
  5. Duplicate phone registration blocked with error "Phone already registered"
  6. OTP expires after 5 minutes; expired OTP shows error with resend option
  7. Max 3 OTP resend attempts per hour per email/phone
  8. Invalid email format rejected with inline validation error

Test Cases

TC-R03Weak password rejectedNoneEnter email + password "password"Validation error listing password requirementsP1
TC-R04Duplicate email blockedjohn@test.com existsRegister with john@test.comError: "Email already registered"P1
TC-R05Duplicate phone blocked+91-9876543210 existsRegister with same phoneError: "Phone already registered"P1
TC-R06OTP expiry — 5 minutesOTP sentWait 6 minutes → Enter OTPError: "OTP expired"; Resend button enabledP1
TC-R07OTP resend limit — 3 per hourOTP sentClick Resend OTP 4 times within 1 hour4th attempt blocked: "Max resend limit reached"P2

FROM users

FROM users
WHERE email = 'john@test.com';
-- Expected: user_count = 1 (not 2 after duplicate attempt)

SELECT otp_code, expires_at, attempts, resend_count, created_at
FROM otp_verifications
WHERE identifier = 'newuser@test.com'
ORDER BY created_at DESC
LIMIT 1;
-- Expected: expires_at = created_at + 5 minutes, resend_count <= 3

-- Verify password is hashed, not plain text
SELECT email, password_hash
FROM users
WHERE email = 'newuser@test.com';
-- Expected: password_hash is bcrypt/argon2 hash, NOT plain text

Scenario 5: API Validation with Database

Requirement

REST API for Product Management supports CRUD operations. Every API response must be validated against database state. DELETE performs soft delete (is_deleted flag) unless forced via query parameter.

User Story with Acceptance Criteria

US-901: Product API CRUD
As an admin user, I want to manage products via REST API, so that the product catalog stays updated.

Acceptance Criteria:
  1. POST /api/products → creates product; returns 201 with product ID and details
  2. GET /api/products/{id} → returns product matching DB record
  3. PUT /api/products/{id} → updates fields; DB reflects changes
  4. DELETE /api/products/{id} → soft delete (is_deleted=1); GET returns 404
  5. DELETE /api/products/{id}?force=true → hard delete; record removed from DB
  6. POST with duplicate SKU → returns 409 Conflict
  7. Unauthorized request (no token) → returns 401

Test Cases

TC IDTest CaseMethodExpected API ResponseDB ValidationPriority
TC-A01Create product — valid payloadPOST /api/products201 Created; body has id, sku, name, priceRow exists in products table with matching valuesP1
TC-A02Get product by IDGET /api/products/{id}200 OK; JSON matches DB recordSELECT returns same data as API responseP1
TC-A03Update product pricePUT /api/products/{id}200 OK; updated price in responseprice column updated; updated_at changedP1
TC-A04Soft delete productDELETE /api/products/{id}204 No Contentis_deleted=1; row still exists; GET returns 404P1
TC-A05Hard delete productDELETE /api/products/{id}?force=true204 No ContentRow completely removed from products tableP2
TC-A06Duplicate SKU rejectedPOST /api/products409 Conflict; error message about duplicate SKUOnly 1 row with that SKU in DBP1
TC-A07Unauthorized accessGET /api/products (no token)401 UnauthorizedNo DB changesP1
TC-A08Get non-existent productGET /api/products/99999404 Not FoundSELECT returns 0 rowsP2

REST Assured Code Snippet

// TC-A01: POST creates product → verify API response → verify DB
@Test
public void testCreateProduct_verifyApiAndDb() {
    String sku = "SKU-TEST-" + System.currentTimeMillis();
    ProductRequest payload = new ProductRequest(sku, "Test Widget", 999.99, 100);

    Response response = given()
        .header("Authorization", "Bearer " + authToken)
        .contentType(ContentType.JSON)
        .body(payload)
    .when()
        .post("/api/products")
    .then()
        .statusCode(201)
        .body("sku", equalTo(sku))
        .body("name", equalTo("Test Widget"))
        .body("price", equalTo(999.99f))
        .body("id", notNullValue())
        .extract().response();

    int productId = response.jsonPath().getInt("id");

    // DB Validation
    Map<String, Object> dbRow = dbHelper.queryForMap(
        "SELECT id, sku, name, price, stock_quantity, is_deleted " +
        "FROM products WHERE id = ?", productId);

    assertEquals(sku, dbRow.get("sku"));
    assertEquals("Test Widget", dbRow.get("name"));
    assertEquals(new BigDecimal("999.99"), dbRow.get("price"));
    assertEquals(0, dbRow.get("is_deleted"));
}

// TC-A04: Soft delete → verify is_deleted flag in DB
@Test
public void testSoftDelete_verifyDbFlag() {
    int productId = createTestProduct();

    given()
        .header("Authorization", "Bearer " + authToken)
    .when()
        .delete("/api/products/" + productId)
    .then()
        .statusCode(204);

    // Verify soft delete in DB
    Map<String, Object> row = dbHelper.queryForMap(
        "SELECT is_deleted FROM products WHERE id = ?", productId);
    assertEquals(1, row.get("is_deleted"));

    // Verify GET returns 404
    given()
        .header("Authorization", "Bearer " + authToken)
    .when()
        .get("/api/products/" + productId)
    .then()
        .statusCode(404);
}

FROM products
WHERE id = 42;
-- Expected: price = 1299.99, updated_at > created_at

-- After soft DELETE: Record exists but flagged
SELECT id, sku, is_deleted, deleted_at
FROM products
WHERE id = 42;
-- Expected: is_deleted = 1, deleted_at IS NOT NULL

-- After hard DELETE: Record gone
SELECT COUNT(*) FROM products WHERE id = 42;
-- Expected: 0

SELECT action, entity_id, old_values, new_values, performed_by, performed_at
FROM audit_log
WHERE entity_type = 'PRODUCT' AND entity_id = 42
ORDER BY performed_at DESC;

Cross-Scenario Interview Tips

When presenting scenarios in interviews:
  1. Start with requirement clarification — show you ask questions before testing
  2. Map each AC to test cases explicitly — interviewers check traceability
  3. Mention both positive and negative test cases — not just happy path
  4. Include DB/API validation for SDET roles — distinguishes senior candidates
  5. Describe Jira workflow naturally — shows real project experience
  6. Prioritize defects by severity and business impact — Critical first
  7. Mention security considerations (PCI DSS, SQL injection, enumeration) proactively

Section 14: Interview Preparation

Comprehensive Q&A bank for QA Automation Engineers (4+ years) targeting Senior QA / SDET roles. Every question includes a detailed answer and what the interviewer expects.

Software Testing — Top 100 Questions

Beginner: Testing Basics (Q1–Q10)

Q1. What is software testing?

Answer: Software testing is the process of evaluating a software product to determine whether it meets specified requirements and to identify defects before release. It involves executing the application under controlled conditions, comparing actual vs expected behavior, and reporting discrepancies. Testing provides stakeholders with information about quality, risk, and readiness for production. It is not just finding bugs—it validates that the system delivers intended business value safely and reliably.

Interviewer expects: A definition beyond "finding bugs"—show you understand testing as risk mitigation and quality assurance.

Q2. Why is software testing necessary?

Answer: Testing reduces the cost of defects by catching issues early when fixes are cheaper. It prevents production failures that damage reputation, revenue, and user trust. Testing validates compliance with requirements, regulations, and SLAs. It also builds confidence for releases, especially in complex systems with integrations. Without testing, teams rely on hope rather than evidence when shipping software.

Interviewer expects: Business impact reasoning—cost, risk, compliance—not just "to find bugs."

Q3. What is the difference between QA and QC?

Answer: Quality Assurance (QA) is process-oriented—it focuses on preventing defects by improving development processes, standards, and practices across the SDLC. Quality Control (QC) is product-oriented—it focuses on identifying defects in the actual product through inspection and testing. QA is proactive; QC is reactive. In practice, QA engineers often do both: they define processes and execute tests.

Interviewer expects: Clear distinction: QA = process/prevention, QC = product/detection.

Q4. What is SDLC?

Answer: Software Development Life Cycle (SDLC) is a structured framework describing phases of software development from inception to retirement. Common phases include requirements, design, development, testing, deployment, and maintenance. SDLC models (Waterfall, Agile, Spiral, etc.) define how these phases are sequenced and iterated. Testing activities are embedded differently depending on the model chosen.

Interviewer expects: Know SDLC phases and that testing is integrated throughout, not a single phase.

Q5. What is STLC?

Answer: Software Testing Life Cycle (STLC) defines the sequence of testing activities: requirement analysis, test planning, test case development, environment setup, test execution, and test cycle closure. Each phase has entry/exit criteria and deliverables (test plan, test cases, RTM, defect reports). STLC runs within SDLC and ensures testing is systematic rather than ad hoc.

Interviewer expects: List STLC phases with deliverables—shows structured testing knowledge.

Q6. What are entry and exit criteria in testing?

Answer: Entry criteria are conditions that must be met before testing can begin (e.g., requirements signed off, build deployed, test environment ready). Exit criteria define when testing can stop (e.g., all P1/P2 test cases passed, defect closure rate met, coverage targets achieved). They prevent premature testing and premature release. Both should be documented in the test plan and agreed with stakeholders.

Interviewer expects: Concrete examples of entry/exit criteria, not vague definitions.

Q7. What is a test plan and what does it contain?

Answer: A test plan is a master document outlining the scope, approach, resources, schedule, and deliverables for a testing effort. Key sections include test objectives, scope (in/out), test strategy, environment requirements, roles, schedule, risks, and entry/exit criteria. It serves as a contract between QA and stakeholders on what will be tested and how. For agile teams, it may be lighter but still exists as a sprint or release test strategy.

Interviewer expects: Mention key sections and link to stakeholder alignment.

Q8. What is a test case?

Answer: A test case is a documented set of preconditions, steps, test data, expected results, and postconditions used to verify a specific requirement or scenario. Good test cases are atomic, repeatable, traceable, and independent. They should include positive, negative, and edge scenarios. Test cases form the basis for manual execution and automation scripts.

Interviewer expects: Know test case components and qualities (traceable, repeatable, independent).

Q9. What is a Requirement Traceability Matrix (RTM)?

Answer: RTM is a document mapping requirements to test cases, ensuring every requirement has test coverage and every test traces back to a requirement. It helps identify gaps (untested requirements) and orphan tests. RTM is updated throughout the project and is critical for audit, compliance, and release sign-off. In agile, traceability may live in Jira links rather than a spreadsheet.
